  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_00dfea59-b3e4-4704-9915-201a227d7815'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer4714384219647828946"><b>The road to power... is paved with blood and magic.<br/><br/>Cleo</b> <i>is now a prisoner in her own palace, forced to be an ambassador for Mytica as the evil King Gaius lies to her people.</i><br/><b>Magnus</b> <i>stands to eventually inherit the new kingdom but is still obsessed with his feelings for his adopted sister, Lucia.</i><br/><b>Lucia</b> <i>is haunted by the outcome of the breathtaking display of magic that allowe</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4714384219647828946" style="display:none"><b>The road to power... is paved with blood and magic.<br /><br />Cleo</b> <i>is now a prisoner in her own palace, forced to be an ambassador for Mytica as the evil King Gaius lies to her people.</i><br /><b>Magnus</b> <i>stands to eventually inherit the new kingdom but is still obsessed with his feelings for his adopted sister, Lucia.</i><br /><b>Lucia</b> <i>is haunted by the outcome of the breathtaking display of magic that allowed her father to capture the kingdoms.</i><br /><b>Jonas</b> <i>watched at the palace gates a troop of rebels behind him, waiting for him to tell them how he plans to overtake King Gaius.</i><br /><br />After a bloody siege, Auranos has been defeated, its young queen orphaned and dethroned. The three kingdoms—Auranos, Limeros, and Paelsia—are now unwillingly united as one country called Mytica. But the allure of ancient, dangerous magic beckons still, and with it the chance to rule not just Mytica, but the whole world over...<br /><br />At the heart of the fray are four brave young people grappling for that magic and the power it promises. For Cleo, the magic would enable her to reclaim her royal seat. In Jonas's hands, it frees his nation, and in Lucia's, it fulfills the ancient prophecy of her destiny. And if the magic were Magnus's, he would finally prove his worth in the eyes of his cruel and scheming father, King Gaius, who rules Mytica with a punishing hand.<br /><br />When Gaius begins to build a road into the Forbidden Mountains to physically link all of Mytica, he sparks a long-smoking fire in the hearts of the people that will forever change the face of this land. For Gaius's road is paved with blood, and its construction will have cosmic consequences.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4714384219647828946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I feel that a lot more happens with the characters and with the story itself in the second book. In fact, imo if you havent read the first book, you c<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I feel that a lot more happens with the characters and with the story itself in the second book. In fact, imo if you havent read the first book, you can definitely start off the series with the second without missing any essential details. And as Kay mentioned, the romance is ridiculous. But if you are able to look past that (takes some effort), then you should be fine.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_483117762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/483117762" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/483117762?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer483117762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5623118685638437260">2 1/2 stars.<br/><br/>I'm honestly not sure if this rating is generous or harsh. I'll let you be the judge.<br/><br/>On the one hand, I couldn't stop myself from coming back to this series after reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12954620.Falling_Kingdoms__Falling_Kingdoms___1_' title='Falling Kingdoms (Falling Kingdoms, #1) by Morgan Rhodes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Falling Kingdoms</a>. <b>Rhodes is an extremely compelling writer</b>. Every scene is crafted in such a way that you're on the edge of your seat, hanging on the author's every word. It's a case of excellent dramatic timing - dragging the scene out with a perfect amount of tension before dropping a dramatic revelation or conclu</span>
  <span id="freeText5623118685638437260" style="display:none">2 1/2 stars.<br /><br />I'm honestly not sure if this rating is generous or harsh. I'll let you be the judge.<br /><br />On the one hand, I couldn't stop myself from coming back to this series after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12954620.Falling_Kingdoms__Falling_Kingdoms___1_" title="Falling Kingdoms (Falling Kingdoms, #1) by Morgan Rhodes" rel="nofollow noopener">Falling Kingdoms</a>. <b>Rhodes is an extremely compelling writer</b>. Every scene is crafted in such a way that you're on the edge of your seat, hanging on the author's every word. It's a case of excellent dramatic timing - dragging the scene out with a perfect amount of tension before dropping a dramatic revelation or conclusion on the reader.<br /><br />And the character dynamics are all exciting. Lots of passions and hatred flowing around, including forbidden relationships, dark secrets, etc. You would think all the aforementioned would add up to a great book, right? <br /><br /><b>Except I simply can't ignore the fact that this is one of the most derivative series I've ever read.</b><br /><br />Literally every major plot point has been borrowed from other fantasy series. I know you can generally expect familiar elements from the genre - royal politics, competing for the throne/power, citizen rebellions - but this goes way beyond that. And the book gets most of its material from - no surprise - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/346732.George_R_R__Martin" title="George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">George R.R. Martin</a>'s <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i>.<br /><br />I can ignore basic setting aspects like the North being all ice and the South being warmer and the general theme of competing for the throne. But King Gaius is like a mash-up of Tywin Lannister and Stannis Baratheon. <br /><br />He takes over Auranos, kills their king, and captures Princess <s>Sansa</s> Cleo, intending to force her to marry his son and future king. However his son - Magnus - has something other than platonic feelings for his sister. Meanwhile, King Gaius is secretly advised by a strange, mystical woman called <s>Lady Melisandre</s> Melenia.<br /><br />Separate from all of this, rebels are coming together to try and overthrow King Gaius and take back their country.<br /><br /><b>I feel like I already know what happens</b>. There is a little part of me that enjoys reading Rhodes' fast-paced, drama-filled plagiarism, but there's a much bigger part that's telling me to go find something better and more original.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/bookgeekreviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5623118685638437260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1931806606" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1931806606" />
    <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net"><img alt="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390032p2/7971097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1931806606?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net">Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1931806606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14985391065655031437"><i>See this review and more at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.bookbastion.net'>www.bookbastion.net</a></i><br/><br/><b>Falling Kingdoms 1:</b> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1362855979?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>★★✩✩✩</a><br/>_______________<br/><br/><b>Incredible. It's somehow even worse than the first one.</b><br/><br/>I'm a patient person but this series tests the limits of that patience in a big way. <b>If I hadn't been reading this as part of a Fantasy League group, I probably would have DNF'ed it.</b> There's simply not enough of value in this discount Game of Thrones to make the journey worth it, and it boggles my mind that it's seen as much success in the YA community as </span>
  <span id="freeText14985391065655031437" style="display:none"><i>See this review and more at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookbastion.net">www.bookbastion.net</a></i><br><br><b>Falling Kingdoms 1:</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1362855979?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">★★✩✩✩</a><br>_______________<br><br><b>Incredible. It's somehow even worse than the first one.</b><br><br>I'm a patient person but this series tests the limits of that patience in a big way. <b>If I hadn't been reading this as part of a Fantasy League group, I probably would have DNF'ed it.</b> There's simply not enough of value in this discount Game of Thrones to make the journey worth it, and it boggles my mind that it's seen as much success in the YA community as the writing just isn't very good. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488370006ra/22105708.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>The plotting in this book is so predictable. It follows a pretty standard formula that repeats itself every 5 chapters or so.</b><br><br><blockquote>🗡️ Cleo reminds someone how terrible her life is - they both cry over the tragedy.<br>🗡️ A character reminds Jonas how perfect he is at everything he does - usually with a declaration of love.<br>🗡️ A character reveals themselves as evil, usually with a monologue about how evil they are. <br>🗡️ Someone related to one of the 3 leads (Cleo, Magnus/Lucia and Jonas,) dies. The person they were closest to cycles every 5 chapters.<br>🗡️ Repeat</blockquote><br>Characterization really goes straight out the window here in favor of cheap surprises meant to shock the reader. Let me make it very clear though: <b>there is a difference between true character growth, and completely altering a character's personality between chapters.</b> It happens multiple times here that a character who was previously defined by one generic set of traits suddenly reveals themselves to be the opposite of those traits and they get to deliver a robotic and cliche-ridden speech about how evil they really are, while I wondered why I was supposed to care. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497719481ra/23052625.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The writing feels emotionally manipulative to me. It's clear Rhodes hasn't plotted this thing out from start to finish, so instead she relies on shock factor and excitement to keep readers invested. <b>Every time things start to get stale, either a death or unexpected romance is thrown in, and then the story spins on in the same cyclical fashion from there.</b> <br><br>___________________<br><br><i>***Since my friend and fellow Fantasy League member, Kaylin, explained this next part better than I did, I'm going to include a link to her review about the treatment of a bisexual character as a plot twist type of reveal near the end of the book.***</i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2000324576?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener"><br>Check her review out here! </a><br><br>___________________<br><br>There's a great deal of pandering too. Such as involving an established straight character in a gay/bisexual subplot 2 chapters from the end, which should tell you how much it factored into the story. <b>Almost like someone informed Rhodes that it's in now to have gay characters in YA books, so instead of crafting a new character she just up and makes a straight character bisexual in the 11th hour to claim diversity points. </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432650890ra/14994085.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
<b>Edit: for the SJWS getting angry: I'm not erasing the fact that bisexuality exists with this complaint.</b> The fact of the matter is - this revelation about this character happens 900+ pages into this series, and there is quite literally <b>NOTHING foreshadowing it. At all.</b> In fact, the reveal itself is played for suspense - Rhodes makes the reader fear for this character's life before he's suddenly being kissed by his would be murderer and it's revealed that he decides he's into it after he just spent 900 pages pining over a woman. I would have zero qualms with the gay/bisexual reveal, if it had been properly developed. Get out of here with your fake outrage and virtue signaling.</blockquote><br><br>Lastly, while no character here is particularly memorable or likable, <b>Jonas remains one of the worst characters ever. I hate him. Hate him, hate him, hate him.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497721406ra/23052798.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>He's clearly Morgan Rhodes' favorite and as such he can do absolutely no wrong. Our Fantasy League took to hashtagging #JustJonasThings (Thanks Kaylin for coming up with the term!) every time Jonas did or said something totally ridiculous - which was all the time. If we had played a drinking game I think we all would have died of alcohol poisoning. <br><br>I just do not get the hype with this series. <b>It has got to be the most overrated, poorly written, popular series I've read this year.</b> I was alternating between 1 and 2 stars again, but I'm settling on 1 this time. Given that this is the second book in the series, I would have expected many of the issues from the first book to be fixed here - but they're not. In fact they're amplified, so I'm settling on 1 star. This series just is not worth the time.<br><br>That being said, the League is forging on and we'll be continuing on with the third book in a few weeks, so keep your eye out for that. <br><br>★✩✩✩✩ = <b>1/5 "read anything else, really," stars</b><br><br>__________________<br><blockquote>A shout out to our Fallen Kingdoms Fantasy League with these fine folk: <br><br>🗡<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/61971658-frankie-lovely" rel="nofollow noopener">Frankie Lovely</a><br>🗡<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary, ~Ravager of Tomes~</a><br>🗡<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/47627265-kaylin" rel="nofollow noopener">Kaylin</a><br>🗡<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/26462337-rachelle" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachelle</a><br>🗡<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17441031-jeremy" rel="nofollow noopener">Jeremy</a>
</blockquote><br>__________________________</span>

<div id="review_2000057458" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2000057458" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2000057458?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2017">year-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2000057458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10974823503371112463"><b>WOW.</b><br/><br/>I mean... <i>what???</i><br/><br/>*coughs* I'm sorry I'm literally just at a loss for words at this moment...<br/><br/><i>
  <b>Just kidding, here are some very disappointed & bitter words for you.</b>
</i><br/><br/>So... <i>by some feat of horrible linguistic gymnastics,</i> this book is actually <b>worse</b> than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12954620.Falling_Kingdoms__Falling_Kingdoms___1_' title='Falling Kingdoms (Falling Kingdoms, #1) by Morgan Rhodes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Falling Kingdoms</a>, which I also gave a 1 star.<br/><br/>I see people say all the time <i>"I would give this book negative stars if I could."</i> Well, this is it for me folks. <b>This is the book I would give negative stars to if I had that capability.</b><br/><br/>I honestly ca</span>
  <span id="freeText10974823503371112463" style="display:none"><b>WOW.</b><br><br>I mean... <i>what???</i><br><br>*coughs* I'm sorry I'm literally just at a loss for words at this moment...<br><br><i>
  <b>Just kidding, here are some very disappointed &amp; bitter words for you.</b>
</i><br><br>So... <i>by some feat of horrible linguistic gymnastics,</i> this book is actually <b>worse</b> than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12954620.Falling_Kingdoms__Falling_Kingdoms___1_" title="Falling Kingdoms (Falling Kingdoms, #1) by Morgan Rhodes" rel="nofollow noopener">Falling Kingdoms</a>, which I also gave a 1 star.<br><br>I see people say all the time <i>"I would give this book negative stars if I could."</i> Well, this is it for me folks. <b>This is the book I would give negative stars to if I had that capability.</b><br><br>I honestly can't decide which aspect of this novel is the worst. Is it the <u>horribly inconsistent characterization?</u> Is it the <u>juvenile writing style?</u> Perhaps the plot that manages to be both <u>choppy &amp; nonexistent at the same time?</u><br><br><b>I guess I'll just ramble about all three &amp; let you guys decide!</b><br><br>So it seems <i>everyone</i> is going to be "in love" with <i>everyone</i> at some point in the series. That in itself is <b>very inconsistent</b> within the parameters of this story. <br><br>We've got characters switching from <i>despising</i> other characters with every fiber of their being to being <b>head over heels in love with them.</b> And it's not even a sexy "enemies-to-lovers" situation. <b>It's a complete &amp; total blindside.</b><br><br>It's <i>"Oh man... 'insert character' sure is hot... Mmm he smells like AXE White Label Body Wash for Men™ even though he hasn't had a bath for weeks... I sure did hate him before but I guess I'm in love with him now, oops."</i><br><br><b>???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????</b><br><br>Am I supposed to be invested in the relationships these characters are forming? This rapidly shifting web of shitty love geometry? Am I suppose to sympathize? Is this a comedy in disguise? <b>Am I misunderstanding a joke here because if I am someone please don't hesitate to fill me in??</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488802386ra/22154260.gif" width="400" height="226" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>On top of this we have characters constantly contradicting their own decisions about who they want to be. I'm not going to spoil this book in my review, <b>but it'll suffice to say that the only characters who truly remain consistent are the most basic, predictably awful, wears-black-to-let-you-know-they're-evil characters.</b> <br><br>Next we've got literally some of <u>the worst writing</u> I think I've ever been exposed to on a professional platform. The dialogue so, so <b>dreadful.</b> <br><br>As with the first book, everyone sounds exactly the same regardless of status, upbringing, age, race, etc. Characters are constantly posturing left &amp; right, puffing up their chests &amp; being defiant with <b>no realistic follow-through action whatsoever.</b><br><br>I've formed a horrible habit of rolling my eyes or saying <i>"Pfft, yea okay, sure buddy."</i> anytime anyone says anything at all. <b>I just do not <i>believeeeeee.</i></b><br><br>It feels like Rhodes' characters desperately want to convince you &amp; themselves that they are a certain way or believe a certain thing, but the result is a lot of <b>head shaking &amp; sarcastic mocking noises on my part.</b><br><br>You end up taking all of the dialogue with the same grain of salt you take a child's statement that they will be an astronaut when they grow up. <br><br>Is it possible that child will be an astronaut? <b>Sure it is!</b> But do you expect that child to understand the kind of realistic, adult trials &amp; tribulations they're committing to to actually become an astronaut? <b>Of course you don't.</b><br><br>The only difference is that my instincts are to be positive &amp; encouraging to that small child in my example, <b>while the only instinctual response these ridiculous characters invoke in me is to backhand them.</b><br><br>But perhaps the <u>most disappointing</u> is the fact that after 800+ pages this plot has gone <b>basically nowhere.</b><br><br>Sure sure, things have happened. <b>But almost nothing <i>interesting</i> has happened!</b><br><br>The plot is <i>so weighed down</i> by the <b>unnecessary angst &amp; contrived inner struggles</b> of these characters. The pieces of the story that do break through the nonsense <b>unfold at an uneven pace</b> &amp; ultimately are <b>so immature</b> that they don't end up mattering enough to improve my reading experience.<br><br>Deaths left &amp; right! But do they matter? <b>No, they do not.</b><br><br>Lots of <i>"DUN DUN DUN"</i> moments that <u>most readers will see coming a mile away.</u><br><br><b>There's just nothing new here.</b><br><br>So far, my experience with this series has been <u>completely uninspired</u> &amp; honestly I don't anticipate the next book will do much to change that fact.<br><br>So why keep reading, you may ask? <br><br><b>Well here's why.</b><br><br>I'm currently participating in a Fantasy League Buddy Read with these lovely folks:<br><br>♥ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/61971658-frankie-lovely" rel="nofollow noopener">Frankie</a><br>♥ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/47627265" rel="nofollow noopener">Kaylin</a><br>♥ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/26462337" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachelle</a><br>♥ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17441031" rel="nofollow noopener">Jeremy</a><br>♥ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7971097" rel="nofollow noopener">Bentley</a><br><br>Each week we guess new ships &amp; deaths. I can only think of one other series where there are <b>so many different ships &amp; deaths</b> that a league like this will make sense, and that is <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i> (which I have no interest in reading at this time, oops shoot me.)<br><br>Anyway, I'm having a wonderful time participating in this league &amp; hearing everyone's thoughts as we read <b>&amp; so unless the next book literally reaches into my chest &amp; crushes my heart</b> I'll be continuing along with this beautiful group of people for as long as I can!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10974823503371112463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1584407459">

<div id="review_1137398207" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1137398207" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1137398207?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1137398207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12226654475933415410">Do you know the feeling when after finishing a good book,it takes some time and considerable effort to adapt to reality again,to make sense of your surroundings and comprehend the sentences that form in the lips of the people around you?When your mind is clouded and refuses to operate and the only thing that matters is to go back in this book,go back where your soul lies?<br/><b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16000044.Rebel_Spring__Falling_Kingdoms___2_' title='Rebel Spring (Falling Kingdoms, #2) by Morgan Rhodes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rebel Spring</a> is one of those books.After I finished it,I could hear people moving and talking,I recognized the need to study,b</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12226654475933415410" style="display:none">Do you know the feeling when after finishing a good book,it takes some time and considerable effort to adapt to reality again,to make sense of your surroundings and comprehend the sentences that form in the lips of the people around you?When your mind is clouded and refuses to operate and the only thing that matters is to go back in this book,go back where your soul lies?<br><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16000044.Rebel_Spring__Falling_Kingdoms___2_" title="Rebel Spring (Falling Kingdoms, #2) by Morgan Rhodes" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebel Spring</a> is one of those books.After I finished it,I could hear people moving and talking,I recognized the need to study,but I just didn't care.Because it was <i>that</i> good.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408122280ra/10809783.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Sometimes,to regain sanity,one had to acknowledge and embrace the madness.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><b>Falling Kingdoms is the Young Adult version of A Song of Ice and Fire,without the explicit sex scenes and the gore.</b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16000044.Rebel_Spring__Falling_Kingdoms___2_" title="Rebel Spring (Falling Kingdoms, #2) by Morgan Rhodes" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebel Spring</a> took us one step further to unraveling the secrets and the meaning of the prophecy about the sorceress and the Kindred in the land of Mytica,which is now ruled by the King of Blood who keeps his people loyal by lying to them and killing anyone who opposes him.The Watchers interfere in the world of the Mortals for their own benefit,everyone has a secret agenda and our 4 heroes still try to figure out their place in their everchanging world.<br><br>One of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5295120.Morgan_Rhodes" title="Morgan Rhodes" rel="nofollow noopener">Morgan Rhodes</a>' best assets is that <b>she doesn't fail to surprise you</b>.There were so many <b>unexpected deaths</b> that I lost count and I had to read it again and again until I accepted what happened.<b>Shocked and shouting profanities was my permanent state!</b>When eveything was peaceful and calm,I got slapped in the face by a <b>plot twist</b>,and not only regarding who lives and who dies.Revelations of schemings and betrayals,romances out of the blue and people doing something out of their character are part of this uncanny ability of Ms.Rhodes.<br><br><b>
  <u>Magnus</u>
</b><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Father and I-we're very much the same.We'll do whatever it takes to get what we want,and we'll hurt whoever gets in our way,no matter who they are.Without conscience or remorse.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Here's a moral question;<b>is it ok to fall in love with the guy who killed the guy I was in love with?</b>Because honestly,I did not see that coming.There are many things that Magnus needs to do to earn his atonement,since every time something atrocious happened in the name of the king he discarded his discomfort as <i>irrelevant</i>,but I deeply hope he will defy the monster he calls his father.He has some moments of humanity that show his heart will not be covered with ice for long.<br><br><b>
  <u>Cleo</u>
</b><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Think of me what you will.But I swear to the goddess I will have my throne back-and King Gaius will pay for his crimes.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>That's my girl!Cleo is still overly confident and naive,I have to admit that,but she started claiming her own fate with her small acts of defiance,and I expect great things from her!<br><br><b>
  <u>Lucia</u>
</b><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“They tell me it's not evil.It doesn't feel evil,really.But there is a darkness taking hold,as if the night itself wraps me in an embrace that grows tighter every moment.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Hmm I <i>think</i> she is going crazy.I liked her in the first book,but she has become so heartless and cruel that she matches her father.And the worst thing is,most of the times she likes that change,she embraces the darkness with open arms.Not a good thing.<br><br><b>
  <u>Jonas</u>
</b><br><br>Nope,I have nothing.He is still an indifferent character,he accomplishes nothing yet he makes it look like he does a lot.There are signs of developement though,so I just have to wait and see.<br><br>But <b>you</b> don't have to wait.You have to go read Falling Kingdoms and discover yourselves!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12226654475933415410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2000324576" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2000324576" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2000324576?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t">finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2000324576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12471344886990771551"><b>1 Star<br/><br/>Overview:</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1815514184' rel='nofollow noopener'>I wasn't</a> a huge fan of the first book. (2/5 stars)<br/><br/>I found the writing cluttered and the dialogue stilted. The plotting sketchy at best, and the character’s inherently unlikable. <br/><br/>But I enjoyed reading it in a fun fantasy league, and thought there was potential. I was really hopeful this book would be a bit better.<br/><br/>...<br/><br/>It got worse, guys. Just <i>so</i> much worse.<br/><br/><b>Pros:</b><br/><br/>*shrug*<br/><br/>I’ve got nothing. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438287980ra/15690349.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Cons:</b><br/><br/>HOLD ON TO YOUR HATS<br/><br/>I present to you, quite possibly the worst line I’ve ever read: (As a euph</span>
  <span id="freeText12471344886990771551" style="display:none"><b>1 Star<br><br>Overview:</b><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1815514184" rel="nofollow noopener">I wasn't</a> a huge fan of the first book. (2/5 stars)<br><br>I found the writing cluttered and the dialogue stilted. The plotting sketchy at best, and the character’s inherently unlikable. <br><br>But I enjoyed reading it in a fun fantasy league, and thought there was potential. I was really hopeful this book would be a bit better.<br><br>...<br><br>It got worse, guys. Just <i>so</i> much worse.<br><br><b>Pros:</b><br><br>*shrug*<br><br>I’ve got nothing. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438287980ra/15690349.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Cons:</b><br><br>HOLD ON TO YOUR HATS<br><br>I present to you, quite possibly the worst line I’ve ever read: (As a euphemism for sex.)<br><i>
  <blockquote> “We’ve shared flesh.</blockquote>
</i><br><br>Is this not just disgusting sounding?? It literally makes me think of The Blob from the 1950s.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1497819883i/23059747._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That plot? That was sketchy before? It’s not sketchy. It’s <i>nonexistent</i>. Everything happens incredibly <i>randomly</i>. Despite having just read this whole book, I feel like NOTHING HAPPENED and we're basically where we started.<br><br>But then everything that does happen is so completely over-the-top-ridiculous. For example:<br><br>-	There’s a literal magic tornado of death that appears out of nowhere and the character’s shrug it off.<br>-	A character decided to start a rebellion by literally approaching random people and asking if they want to join his rebellion. <br>-	The horribly evil king who supposedly slaughters without remorse spends time telling his teenage son all of his plans<br>-	Two female characters have a “who-suffered-more” contest where they bemoan their horrible circumstances and end up in tears.<br>-	A character who was present for <i>3-pages</i> of the first book is brought back to be killed in dramatic fashion. <br>-	Every single female character is entranced by Jonas’ beauty and immediately loves him. <br><br>At one point, a character literally decides to cauterize his own wound. I’m sure this was supposed to make him look badass and impress the lady he’s with—but it’s so medically inaccurate it hurts. The character feels the bleeding from his arm is significant enough to require cauterization, but he spends time talking about it first, doesn’t attempt to hold pressure or stop the bleeding, shows no signs of shock and remains completely composed as he grabs his dirty knife from his pocket to do it. IT’S ALL SO RIDICULOUS I CAN’T EVEN.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497820992ra/23059800.gif" width="325" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>All of the characters are absolutely pathetic. There's no motivation for anyone’s actions. Every so often Rhodes will kill a random side-character that supposedly spurs one of our main-characters to action, as if that’s the only sort of motivating factor people are capable of?<br><br>Then towards the end, things went from just kind of ridiculous to full-on-awful. First off, a male-character we’ve been familiar with since book one is kissed by another man and enjoys it. <br><br>(Before we go any further, <u>my problem is not the characters sexuality.</u> I am <i>literally</i> bisexual myself. I don’t believe a character should be necessarily assumed straight because they’ve shown preference for opposite sex so far.)<br><br>If the character was kissed by another man, surprised to find he liked it and had to reevaluate himself and what he wants—I could get behind it. It’s not winning any Pulitzers, but it would have required introspection and actual character development.<br><br>What I'm NOT okay with is how the whole scene is written. <br><br>- This random man encourages our-character to get drunk, continually buying him drinks. (<i>"more drinks for my friend here!"</i>)<br>- This man makes our-character FEAR for his life and follows him when he tries to leave.<br>- This man continues to frighten our character ON PURPOSE. (<i> "You're afraid of me..." he moved closer still. )</i><br><br>Our character reports he’s had 10-15 glasses of fermented rice-wine. (Which wikipedia tells me has an alcohol content of 18%-25%) Do you really think he could consent to anything???<br><br>This isn't some big scene that causes a crisis of sexuality. It literally reads like sexual assault. This stranger physically intimidates our impaired character before surprise kissing him and then insisting that the character enjoyed the kiss so much it just opened new worlds. It's gross. And it's even more disgusting that this was how Rhodes decided to add a shred of diversity to her massive cast. <br><br>As if that wasn’t bad enough, THE VERY NEXT CHAPTER includes an attempted rape scene. A female character is literally introduced for the <i>sole</i> purpose of being sexually assaulted by one of the “bad guys” so we can be reminded how evil he is and won’t mourn him when he dies two pages later. <br><br>Guys there’s quasi-incest in this that’s less disgusting. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497820992ra/23059801.gif" width="400" height="190" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>In Conclusion: </b><br><br>As awful as this was, I enjoyed reading it in a fun-fantasy league with these lovely people! They are all hilarious and sweet, and the only thing that motivated me to finish this. <br><br>* The bunny mama who keeps us all organized, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/61971658-frankie-lovely" rel="nofollow noopener"> Frankie!</a> <br><br>* The one who unlocked Rhodes' entire writing formula, <a>Bentley!</a><br><br>* The ball of rage who hates everyone pretty equally, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary!</a><br><br>* My medical buddy, who agrees that cauterization was ridiculous,<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/26462337-rachelle" rel="nofollow noopener"> Rachelle! </a> <br><br>* The only one of us who liked the first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Jeremy!</a><br><br>I'm glad we are taking a break before continuing on, because my mind needs it. At this point I'm just hoping it can't get worse.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12471344886990771551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1819785213" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1819785213" />
    <a title="L A i N E Y" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y"><img alt="L A i N E Y" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546138360p2/10752235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1819785213?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L A i N E Y" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L A i N E Y" href="/user/show/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y">L A i N E Y</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3009983789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9967263377928511602"><b>4.75 Golden Stars</b><br/><br/><i>May the last book of 2019 be a Five-Star!</i><br/><br/><i>6th best of 2019</i><br/><br/>I don't lie if I say I wanted to give it 4 stars until the last 10-15 chapters as I was back in the mood for this world again; all those events! It totally deserved 5 in the end.<br/>it was definitely better than the first book, the characters met & their stories crossed; so many excitements & sarcasm! I laughed a lot & smirked a lot by their wits.<br/><br/>the whole plot was interesting & exciting, the way I like, the end was fantastic,</span>
  <span id="freeText9967263377928511602" style="display:none"><b>4.75 Golden Stars</b><br /><br /><i>May the last book of 2019 be a Five-Star!</i><br /><br /><i>6th best of 2019</i><br /><br />I don't lie if I say I wanted to give it 4 stars until the last 10-15 chapters as I was back in the mood for this world again; all those events! It totally deserved 5 in the end.<br />it was definitely better than the first book, the characters met &amp; their stories crossed; so many excitements &amp; sarcasm! I laughed a lot &amp; smirked a lot by their wits.<br /><br />the whole plot was interesting &amp; exciting, the way I like, the end was fantastic, intriguing &amp; shocking. I could jump into the 3rd book.<br />the only flaw (beside being dragged at some points) was:<br />I wanted more Magnus!<br /><br />a few words to the characters:<br /><br />"please love Magnus!<br />don't you see he's under how much pressure!?<br />he has to act like this!<br />&amp; he was grown up by the hands of king of Blood.<br />he is the heir!<br />&amp; it's obvious he's different than him! (why can't you see it?)<br />the way he'd been surprised (but hid it in an instant) by the acts of his surroundings.<br />but he knows, I know he knows... I see, I feel!<br />Pleaseeeee Understand him!"<br /><br />that's probably my ultimate goal in this series!<br />thank you very much!<br /><br />the character developments were strong; the choices they made, the way they acted.<br />the Prince is changing. (slowly, but certainly)<br />the Rebel, being braver, stronger &amp; more leader-like.<br /><b>Re-read 2020</b>: Cleo still could make me angry, but I like her now, she's determined &amp; strong. but Lucia is still annoying &amp; so much like Gaius.<br /><br /><br />World building: ★★★★/5<br />Characters: ★★★★(★)/5<br />Writing style: ★★★★/5<br />Plot: ★★★★(★)/5<br />General idea: ★★★★★/5<br />-<br />check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2279447572" rel="nofollow noopener">Falling Kingdom review</a> of mine for more details</span>

<div id="review_1231053748" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1231053748" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1231053748?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Anne by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1171076-danielle-long">Danielle Long</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=recommended-by-a-not-stupid-friend">recommended-by-a-not-stupid-friend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=mature-ya">mature-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1231053748" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer524990027813642475">Well, I'm back for Round 2 of this series that my Pushy Librarian is making me read!<br/><i>If you don't have a Pushy Librarian of your own, I highly recommend you get one. Mine is very sweet once you get to know her...</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429609879ra/14611784.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The first book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/475352100' rel='nofollow noopener'>Falling Kingdoms</a>, was a total bloodbath. Main characters that I thought would make it to the end of the series weren't any safer than the minor characters who barely had time to say OUCH! before someone killed them off. So, I was kinda expecting the same thing to happen in</span>
  <span id="freeText524990027813642475" style="display:none">Well, I'm back for Round 2 of this series that my Pushy Librarian is making me read!<br><i>If you don't have a Pushy Librarian of your own, I highly recommend you get one. Mine is very sweet once you get to know her...</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429609879ra/14611784.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/475352100" rel="nofollow noopener">Falling Kingdoms</a>, was a total bloodbath. Main characters that I thought would make it to the end of the series weren't any safer than the minor characters who barely had time to say OUCH! before someone killed them off. So, I was kinda expecting the same thing to happen in Rebel Spring.<br>Ha!<br>The author changed it up on me, and I got lulled into a false sense of security. Not very many people bite it in this one, but when they did? I didn't see it coming. <br>I would be all, <i>La-la-la-la-la!</i>, and then<b> BOOM! CRACK! SNAP!</b><br><i>Wait. What?! Really? Did he just twist her head off?! </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429625920ra/14613343.gif" width="350" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Did that really happen in the story? Eh. I may be exaggerating. <i>A tad.</i><br>But, this one is a true story:<br>I had just read the part where a knife is sliding into the heart of one of the Main Characters, and all I needed to do was turn the page to see how it all turned out. And I swear, the alarm on my phone goes off to let me know it's time to get in the car &amp; pick up the kids from school, <b>or I'll be late</b>.<br>I actually sat there for a few seconds thinking to myself...<br><i>Would it REALLY kill them to be the last kids picked up. I'm never late. Maybe they'd appreciate me more if they had to sweat it this one time? It could be a learning experience for them!</i><br>In the end, even a slack parent like myself couldn't rationalize it, but I came close. Real close.<br>Does that make me a bad mom?<br>Maybe. But you know what I tell my kids?<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429628258ra/14613741.gif" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really think this series may be perfect for me.<br>You have multiple POVs going on, with each story telling a different side to the main plot. And there are honestly too many for me to go into detail with each one. The main ones I'm riveted by are Magnus and Cleo. Especially Magnus. He's the son of the evil king who has just forcibly taken over two other kingdoms. This dude has serious issues going on in his personal life. Not the least of which are his unrequited feelings toward his adopted sister. <br>Now, normally, I'd be all horrified and disgusted by this.<br>Because...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429631482ra/14614188.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But Rhodes manages to keep him from feeling like a total scumbag. By the end of this book, I was actually rooting for him, because it seems like he may be on the verge of going in a different direction. In fact, almost every character is wildly different than they were when we first met them. That's not to say they all got personality transplants, but it seems like they are growing and changing in a natural way. Each one influenced by their own experiences during the course of the story. <br>Very cool! <br><br>Another thing I'm enjoying about this is the distinct lack of Twue Wuv as something that moves the plot. And now that I think about it, <i>nobody</i> in the entire book is having much luck in the love department. <br>It's one long list that looks like this:<br>He-Loves-Her-But-She-Loves-Someone-Else-And-They-Ain't-Interested.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429631872ra/14614260.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'd like to go on and on about his one, but the truth is, I have the next book sitting on my coffee table right now. <br>If you're looking for a YA Game of Thrones sort of tale, then check this out!</span>
  <a data-text-id="524990027813642475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

</a><br/><br/><br/>I need to know what happens, I need the third book like air. <b>I NEED IT</b>. NOW!<br/><br/><br/>After careful consideration, I think I liked Rebel Spring better than the FK, however some things just didn't convince me at all, hence 4 stars instead of 5.   <span id="freeText17392733008593226483" style="display:none">AAAHAGSHSHSVSVSHSVSHSVSUSVSJSBSISHSVSHSVSUSVSUSVSUVSHSVSISVSIIDBSOHMYGODDDDDDD<br><br>Pardon my French but HOLY FUCK! What was that? Do you seriously call that <i>an ending</i>???<br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/M4qy" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1507537181ra/24124444.gif" alt="467bl.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>I need to know what happens, I need the third book like air. <b>I NEED IT</b>. NOW!<br><br><br>After careful consideration, I think I liked Rebel Spring better than the FK, however some things just didn't convince me at all, hence 4 stars instead of 5. Fortunately <i>pour vous et pour moi</i>, it's the kind of things one can easily overcome by wearing super useful fanbase goggles and squinting a little over the cheesiness and the eye-rolling plot escapes. <br>I even read it all in one sitting, can you believe how much it got me whipped? Like, my eyes are dry and burning but it's okay, my brain would like to let you guys know that it was <b>totally worth it</b>. <br><br>Rhodes writes nice dialogues, I'll give it to her. My favorite exchanges were between Cleo and Magnus. I love it when she puts him in his place. <br>To be honest, I haven't being paying much attention to the technical details, but I found the writing a little bit better this time around. Can't say the same for the character development (except for Cleo. Cleo is perfect. No, shh, I can't hear you over the sound of her greatness) of the entire cast, but I suppose it's only fair since this series is 6 books long and there's still so much to learn (hashtag watch me defend my fave 2k17). <br><br>Anyway... <br>By now, I consider this series my guilty pleasure. You know, those books a lot of people like to make fun of but that you secretly (not so secretly in my case) adore? Those books you're not particularly proud of enjoying because they're just so self-indulgent they make you wanna cry or punch SOMEONE, but that you enjoy anyway because who cares what the mass think? Well, this is mine. <br>It's not perfect and it probably never will br, but it made me feel things while I was reading it. I was happy while reading it. Popular or not popular, loved or hated, when it comes to books, I think that's the most important thing.<br><br>So, yeah, this is another YES, for me. Can't wait to see how everything blows up in the next one.<br>Gimme all the feels!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2323541005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16942203579149004321"><u>3.5 The road to power... is paved with blood and magic. ★'s</u> <br/><br/><i>“I believe we make our own destinies, every last one of us.” </i><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522711566i/25313909._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> I hate that i'm having to say this, but I didn't like "Rebel Spring" quite as much as as I did <i>Falling Kingdoms</i>... and sadly i'm not as excited as I originally was for this series :( I had such high hopes going into the second book and I was let down. I really hope <i>Gathering Darkness</i> will be able to restore my hopes in this series! One of the things I really didn't like is th</span>
  <span id="freeText16942203579149004321" style="display:none"><u>3.5 The road to power... is paved with blood and magic. ★'s</u> <br><br><i>“I believe we make our own destinies, every last one of us.” </i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522711566i/25313909._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> I hate that i'm having to say this, but I didn't like "Rebel Spring" quite as much as as I did <i>Falling Kingdoms</i>... and sadly i'm not as excited as I originally was for this series :( I had such high hopes going into the second book and I was let down. I really hope <i>Gathering Darkness</i> will be able to restore my hopes in this series! One of the things I really didn't like is the <i>"romantic relationships"</i> between some of the characters. It really bugs me because it comes out of nowhere, it's like all of a sudden <b>BAM</b> they love each other!!! And i'm left confused because there was no indication of such feelings or even attraction toward one another. For real though, I didn't see any signs of these said feelings/attractions. So yeahhh, That bothers me a lot! Also every guy we get introduced to seems to always be in love with Princess Cleo or with Princess Lucia. Other than these things, I did still enjoy the plot, the writing style, the character and the world building. I think it skimmed over things to quickly, such as the wedding tour. I think there should have been more to it! I still love Cleo and I really wished she would have been in this one much more. I honestly think shes my favorite character :D I know everyone loves Magnus but as of now, i'm not entirely sure how i'm feeling about the dark prince. He has this unhealthy obsession for his sister and then he has this fake facade put up all the time and all the while, I'm still sitting here waiting for him to grow a pair! There were a few more deaths and one of them, I was happy about! Ugh... I hated that little bastard!! But perhaps because he was so well hated he should have stuck around?? IDK. Okay well anyways, now i'm onto book #3, I so hope it's better. <br><br><b>*I do love this cover though :D*</b> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522711566i/25313909._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“She gripped the front of his shirt. It was all too much--she wasn't sure if she was pushing him away or pulling him closer. Much like diving into deep water, she had no idea which way would find her air to breathe or which way would drag her down deeper into the depths where she would surely drown.<br><br>And for a moment, just a moment, she found it didn't seem to matter.”</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474183132ra/20564548.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“But even the coldest hate can shift into something warmer if given enough time, just as an ugly caterpillar can turn into a beautiful butterfly.”</i></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1766388273?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1766388273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5492389164626211624">I expected <i>way</i> more from this book but I still loved it a lot mostly because i know that this series is going to be great. Before I get into the actual review here’s my reactions and feelings towards characters,<br/>(edit before gathering darkness)<br/>Me falling for Magnus in this book:<br/><a href='http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/giphy_zpsisrb5enl.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

  <span id="freeText5492389164626211624" style="display:none">I expected <i>way</i> more from this book but I still loved it a lot mostly because i know that this series is going to be great. Before I get into the actual review here’s my reactions and feelings towards characters,<br>(edit before gathering darkness)<br>Me falling for Magnus in this book:<br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/giphy_zpsisrb5enl.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br>ILY Jonas, but me whenever I saw his plans:<br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/joeydoor_zpsregguxoi.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479725857ra/21227100.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_inline_myopczABXg1r3myp8_zpsj8uegeiy.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Gaius, the father of the year award recipient:<br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/tumblr_n6ebhkU9wy1sncnhgo1_500_zpsqf8ibftn.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479725857ra/21227101.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_n6ebhkU9wy1sncnhgo1_500_zpsqf8ibftn.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Me with the watchers:<br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/justin-where-are-you-gif_zpsfe5sgd93.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479725857ra/21227102.gif" alt=" photo justin-where-are-you-gif_zpsfe5sgd93.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>This book was both underwhelming and overwhelming at once if that even makes sense. It was such a fun ride with all the ups and downs that the first book had. It has you at the edge of your seat since the very beginning. This book I think is kind of a bridge book, that is just furthering the plot and making way for better storylines in the future. That being said, nothing exactly happens in this book especially when you compare it to Falling Kingdoms. That does not mean that you won’t have a fun time reading this. There is something seriously so addictive about these books that will hook you and won’t let you go till the end. <br>This plot as said in the synopsis, is focused more on the road that is being built to bridge all of Mytica together. There is a deeper reason behind this that will come into play in the future books and I am really excited to see where it heads. The kingdoms are slowly starting to come together especially since Gaius takes over everything and is now officially ruling over the entire Mytica. The characters are also starting to come together, and I can finally see their storylines intertwine a little and I am so glad that it is happening. <br>The characters are growing so much and honestly I’m starting to love them and understand their motives and feeling that drive them. This book does show a lot of growth for the characters and I’m happy that I’m finally starting to understand them! <br>As shown before, I’m definitely a Magnus fan as of now which I was not in the first book. I truly get to see the emotions that he has and what goes on inside him, while he puts up an icy exterior as a mask. Cleo is starting to get way more understand-able and I’m seeing the good qualities in her that I could not spot in the first book, she is going to make a great queen (in the coming books, I hope). Lucia was always an interesting character and we see her go through massive changes in this book that I’m quite surprised about! Honestly, I can’t wait to see what happens to her in the next books. Jonas was my favorite in the first book, but I feel as though his position has been usurped by the one and only Magnus. Jonas kind of takes to the shadows and this was kind of disappointing (his plans were even more disappointing). I hope his character gets explored more in the next few books.<br><br><br><b>
  <i>WARNING, spoilery talk from here</i>
</b><br><br><br>This book might have been less interesting from the previous one but it still had its fair share of drama, that I obviously enjoyed. It was so surprising to think that Cleo and Magnus were going to be <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ engaged  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I understand why Gaius would have wanted it to happen but it was literally announced in the first chapter I believe. <br>It was so interesting to see the character dynamics of Cleo and Magnus together. Both are so very different but if you put them together, I’m sure they will make a really really adorable couple. I knew what was coming for them (curtesy to spoilers :/) but still when their <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[marriage happened after the magical earthquake,  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I was so surprised, I mean I at least thought it would have been done later lmao. But when it did happen I was just there like,<br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/giphy_zpsr1jn5pyw.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479725857ra/21227103.gif" alt=" photo giphy_zpsr1jn5pyw.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>	<br>The minor run in the woods that happened was kind of awkward for me. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Sure, Jonas and Cleo kissed once, but like Jonas pretty much fell in love with her after that which was weird, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I expected it to happen, but I didn’t expect to be so indifferent about it.<br>Also what on earth is happening to Lucia’s character. What happened to the sweet and caring girl from Book 1?? <br><br>Despite, there not being anything much, this was still an amazing sequel and I’m sure this series is going to keep on getting better book by book.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5492389164626211624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1549303872" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1549303872?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1549303872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14630637082149478010"><blockquote>
  <i>❝Evil is a choice one makes, not a natural state of being.❞</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I'm not gonna take my time on this one and this review will be a lot shorter than most reviews. I'm just gonna get to the point: <b>Rebel Spring was a lot more boring than Falling Kingdoms.</b> Fallings Kingdoms was actually not boring and I actually gave it a rating of 4.5 stars simply because I am not a fan of incest so that kind of dragged it a little tiny bit. But other than that, I found Morgan's writing phenomenal and I loved the high</span>
  <span id="freeText14630637082149478010" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>❝Evil is a choice one makes, not a natural state of being.❞</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I'm not gonna take my time on this one and this review will be a lot shorter than most reviews. I'm just gonna get to the point: <b>Rebel Spring was a lot more boring than Falling Kingdoms.</b> Fallings Kingdoms was actually not boring and I actually gave it a rating of 4.5 stars simply because I am not a fan of incest so that kind of dragged it a little tiny bit. But other than that, I found Morgan's writing phenomenal and I loved the high fantasy and magic elements in the novel. <i>Rebel Spring</i> was quite different and even though I don't consider it my favorite, I'm pretty sure I'm gonna like the other 2 books because I have heard the series gets a lot better. <br /><br /><i>Rebel Spring</i> dealt with some love triangles. And just like my friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/44137919" rel="nofollow noopener">Mikee</a> has said:<br /><i>Magnus is still figuring out his feelings for his adopted sister Lucia while growing feelings for Cleo at the same time. Theo and Aron were in love with Cleo as well and even though Aron still says he wants her back and loves her, I was always sure the love was doubted and not real. Nic has always had a soft side for Cleo and has always been one of her best friends that have been with her but sometimes I wasn't able to tell her if he loves her or</i> <b>loves</b> <i>her. Cleo fell for Jonas but can't help the feelings she's growing for Magnus. Jonas fell in love with Cleo but at the same time he wants to be with Lyssandra. Lucia fell in love with Alexius right away but isn't really in love with Magnus, only loves him as a brother.</i><br /><br />I didn't have any problems with the "love triangles" since I actually know who is gonna end up with who (damn it spoilers.) There weren't much surprises and shocking moments since I had a feeling of what came, was about to happen. There are 4 main characters and I think everyone knows they aren't gonna die or are supposed to. There was a lot of violence in Falling Kingdoms so I wasn't completely amazed by the other deaths. In fact, I was happy at times. I was glad Morgan decided to kill some of her characters because they actually deserved it and I <s>probably</s> hated them since the beginning so I didn't pay much attention or showed no interest. I didn't particularly enjoy Jonas' point of views as well except for the "shocking" ones including moments with Cleo and fighting scenes. I will admit I was able to ship Jonas and Cleo more than Cleo and Magnus but... <br /><br />As a conclusion, I'm gonna end up finishing the series just because I want to see how these <b>ships</b> work out and even though I know who ends up with who, I luckily haven't spoiled myself in reading <b>how</b> it all works out and how that person ended up with <b>that</b> person.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14630637082149478010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17364686439311115714"><b> 4.5 stars! </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “Evil is a choice one makes, not a natural state of being.” </i> </b><br/><br/>So I don't usually do this, but this review is going to be told mostly in gifs. To be more specific, Mean Girls gifs. The land has transformed into one where no one is safe and survival is not easy. The king has become crazy with the notion that magic will further</span>
  <span id="freeText17364686439311115714" style="display:none"><b> 4.5 stars! </b><br><br><b> <i> “Evil is a choice one makes, not a natural state of being.” </i> </b><br><br>So I don't usually do this, but this review is going to be told mostly in gifs. To be more specific, Mean Girls gifs. AWWWW YEAAAHHHHH!!!!!<br><br>Me while reading this series:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453783187ra/17870905.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After the events of the previous book, three kingdoms have become one under the rule of the tyrant King Gaius. The land has transformed into one where no one is safe and survival is not easy. The king has become crazy with the notion that magic will further his power and he is doing everything he can to work magic into his own plans. <br><br><b> Jonas </b> has become the leader of the rebellion against King Gaius who was once his ally. He got better in this book than the last but he seemed to make some decisions. <br>This was Jonas throughout the book with his revenge plans:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453783254ra/17870911.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> Lucia </b> spends the majority of her time in a powerful sleep (aka coma) and also struggles with the attentions of Magnus. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453783754ra/17870929.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am joining Jasmine and Christine in the I Hate Lucia club of which I declare myself the treasurer.<br>Seriously this gif describes her perfectly:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453783754ra/17870930.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> Magnus </b> oh that beautiful man. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453783754ra/17870931.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So tortured and misunderstood by those around him.
